<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Rugby League World Cup</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>Rugby League World Cup</b>  is an international <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> tournament, contested by national teams of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_International_Federation" title="Rugby League International Federation">Rugby League International Federation</a>, which was first held in France in <a href="/wiki/1954_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1954 Rugby League World Cup">1954</a>, the first World Cup in either <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby code</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Folkard03-337_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Folkard03-337-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The idea of a rugby league world cup tournament was first mooted in the 1930s with the French proposal to hold a tournament in 1931, and again in 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The fifteen tournaments held to date have been at intervals ranging from two to eight years, and have featured a number of formats.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> So far three nations have won the competition (<a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a> eleven times, <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> three times and New Zealand once). Australia, France and New Zealand are the only teams to have played in all tournaments (Great Britain has been split into <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Scotland national rugby league team">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a> since 1995, while England and Wales had previously competed as separate teams in the 1975 World Cup). Since 2000, the RLIF has also organised World Cups for <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Women&#39;s Rugby League World Cup">women</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_Student_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Tertiary Student Rugby League World Cup">students</a> and <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_World_Cups" title="Festival of World Cups">other categories</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017 Rugby League World Cup</a> was held in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> which was won by <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1935.E2.80.931954:_Establishment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1935–1954:_Establishment">1935–1954: Establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1935–1954: Establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Rugby League World Cup was an initiative of the French who had been campaigning for a competition since 1935. The idea was raised in 1951 by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Barri%C3%A8re" title="Paul Barrière">Paul Barrière</a>, the President of the <a href="/wiki/French_rugby_league_championship" class="mw-redirect" title="French rugby league championship">French Rugby League</a>. In 1952, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a> secretary <a href="/wiki/Bill_Fallowfield" title="Bill Fallowfield">Bill Fallowfield</a> persuaded the Rugby League Council to support the concept.<sup id="cite_ref-Waddingham14-06-08_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waddingham14-06-08-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> At a meeting in <a href="/wiki/Blackpool" title="Blackpool">Blackpool</a>, England in 1953, the <a href="/wiki/International_Rugby_League_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="International Rugby League Board">International Board</a> accepted Paul Barrière’s proposal that France should be the nation to host<sup id="cite_ref-Waddingham14-06-08_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waddingham14-06-08-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> the first tournament to be officially
known as the "Rugby World Cup".<sup id="cite_ref-SPARC-2009-p28_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPARC-2009-p28-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the hosts, the tournament featured teams from Britain, Australia and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1954_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1954 Rugby League World Cup">1954 Rugby League World Cup</a> was won by Great Britain who defeated France in Paris on 13 November to claim the title.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dave_Valentine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a0/Dave_Valentine.jpg/170px-Dave_Valentine.jpg" width="170" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a0/Dave_Valentine.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="180" data-file-height="220" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dave_Valentine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Captain of the winning British team, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Valentine" title="Dave Valentine">Dave Valentine</a>, presented with the trophy at the inaugural World Cup in 1954</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="1955.E2.80.931974:_Sporadic_competitions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1955–1974:_Sporadic_competitions">1955–1974: Sporadic competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1955–1974: Sporadic competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The World Cup was initially contested by the four Test nations: <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_league_team" title="France national rugby league team">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a>. The teams played each other in a <a href="/wiki/Sports_league" title="Sports league">league</a> format.  A final match was played between the top two teams in 1954.  It was then decided that the team that finished first in the league would be declared the winner at the second World Cup in 1957, when Australia proved victorious on their home ground.
</p><p>After the successful 1960 competition, in which Great Britain won the title for the second time, there would be no further World Cup for eight years. The competition had been scheduled to be held in France in 1965, this time with the inclusion of the <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_rugby_league_team" title="South Africa national rugby league team">South African team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> However, after an unsuccessful tour of Australia, the French withdrew. The tournament was next held in 1968, and followed a two-year cycle until the mid-1970s.
</p><p>The 1972 World Cup final ended in 10-all, and the title was awarded to Great Britain by virtue of their superior record in the qualifiers. Great Britain were captained by Welshman, <a href="/wiki/Clive_Sullivan" title="Clive Sullivan">Clive Sullivan</a> who was the first black player to captain any British national sports team.
</p>
<h3><span id="1975.E2.80.931990s:_International_hosts"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1975–1990s:_International_hosts">1975–1990s: International hosts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1975–1990s: International hosts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1975, the competition underwent a radical overhaul. It was decided to play matches on a home and away basis around the world instead of one host nation and the Great Britain team was split into England and Wales meaning that the tournament would be increased from the 4 teams of previous tournaments to 5, this number also taking part in the two future internationally held tournaments. There was not a final held to decide the champions of the 1975 tournament and so Australia won by virtue of topping the group standings.  As Australia had not beaten England in that tournament a '<a href="/wiki/1975_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1975 Rugby League World Cup">final challenge match</a>' was hastily arranged which Australia would win 25-0.  
</p><p>In 1977 it was decided that Great Britain should once more compete as a single entity. Although the final between Australia and Great Britain was a closely fought affair, public interest in the tournament waned due to the continuing tinkering with the format and it was not held again until the mid-1980s.
</p><p>From 1985 to 1988, each nation played each other a number of times on a home and away basis with a number of these games also being considered part of various international tours that took place during the years in which these world cups were being played.  At the end of that period, Australia met New Zealand at <a href="/wiki/Eden_Park" title="Eden Park">Eden Park</a>. The match was a physical encounter, and Australian captain <a href="/wiki/Wally_Lewis" title="Wally Lewis">Wally Lewis</a> played part of the match with a broken arm. The Kangaroos won the competition 25-12. 
</p><p>This format was repeated from 1989–1992 (with games once again also being part of tours) and Australia won again, defeating Great Britain 10-6 at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1924)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wembley Stadium (1924)">Wembley Stadium</a> in front of 73,361 people. This crowd remained a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup_records" title="Rugby League World Cup records">Rugby League World Cup record</a> (and a record for any rugby league international match) until beaten by the 74,468 crowd which attended the 2013 World Cup Final at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The fifth nation to compete in these two tournaments was Papua New Guinea.
</p>
<h3><span id="1995.E2.80.932008:_Knockout_tournament_and_expansion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1995–2008:_Knockout_tournament_and_expansion">1995–2008: Knockout tournament and expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1995–2008: Knockout tournament and expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby League World Cup">1995</a>, the competition was once again restructured, returning to the traditional 'host' format with ten teams entering. Unlike previous tournaments where the top two teams in the table playing in the final, a knockout stage was added with a quarter and semi final. New teams competing included <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> and South Africa. Due to the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_war" title="Super League war">Super League war</a>, players aligned with the rebel competition were not selected by the ARL to represent the Kangaroos. This meant the absence of many star players from the Australian team's line-up. The tournament, which was also held to celebrate the centenary of the sport in England, was highly successful with over 250,000 people attending the group stages and over 66,000 people attending the final to see Australia defeat England 16-8.
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Super_League_war" title="Super League war">Super League war</a>, the subsequent re-structuring of rugby league's international governing bodies meant that the proposed 1998 World Cup was postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2000_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2000 Rugby League World Cup">2000 World Cup</a> expanded the field further, with sixteen teams entering.  This tournament included a <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_M%C4%81ori_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand Māori rugby league team">New Zealand Maori</a> representative team, the only time this team has taken part.  However numerous issues including poor organization and blown-out scorelines meant that this tournament was seen as highly unsuccessful with an average attendance just half that of the previous tournament.  Due to these problems the competition was put on indefinite hiatus. Australia won the tournament by beating New Zealand 40-12 in the final at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>.  In the same year, the first <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Women&#39;s Rugby League World Cup">Women's Rugby League World Cup</a> was held with New Zealand defeating Great Britain.
</p><p>The World Cup returned in <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008</a> with a 10-team format. Australia hosted the tournament and New Zealand were crowned champions for the first time by beating the host nation at <a href="/wiki/Lang_Park" title="Lang Park">Lang Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>.  The world cup was once again seen as a success with a 91% average attendance increase on the previous competition.  New Zealand became only the third team to win the world cup and the first other than Australia since 1972.
</p>
<h3><span id="2009.E2.80.93present:_Regular_competition"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009–present:_Regular_competition">2009–present: Regular competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2009–present: Regular competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 tournament</a>, hosted by England and Wales, expanded to 14 teams and was considered the most successful competition to date in terms of attendances, exposure and financial output. Australia took the title again after defeating New Zealand in the final by a score of 34–2.  The final attendance became the record international rugby league attendance at 74,468.  
</p><p>Following the 2013 tournament, it was decided that the world cup would be scheduled to take place every four years, <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017 Rugby League World Cup</a> taking place in Australia, New Zealand and for the first time in Papua New Guinea.  While Australia would claim the title once again and for an eleventh time, the tournament was considered highly successful in terms of competitiveness.  The tournament would see Tonga beat New Zealand in the group stages with a score of 28-22 to top the group, the first time a team from outside the top 3 had beaten a top 3 nation in over two decades.  New Zealand went on to play Fiji in the quarter-finals and lost once again with a score of just 4-2, knocking New Zealand out in the quarter-finals, the first time a tier 1 nation had exited the tournament at this early stage.  Tonga played England in the semi-finals and while conceding 20 unanswered points, they would score 3 tries in just the last seven minutes to pull the score back to 20-18, eventually losing by this close margin.  The final was contested between Australia and England at <a href="/wiki/Lang_Park" title="Lang Park">Lang Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> and Australia won by just 6-0, the lowest score in world cup final history.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>	
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2021_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2021 Rugby League World Cup">2021 tournament</a> will be held in England with organisers expressing a desire to see a total of one million fans attend games.  This tournament will see the number of teams increased to 16 once again.  The 2025 Rugby League World Cup will be held in the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophy">Trophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Trophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup_Trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League World Cup Trophy">Rugby League World Cup Trophy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RLWC_trophy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/RLWC_trophy.jpg/150px-RLWC_trophy.jpg" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/RLWC_trophy.jpg/225px-RLWC_trophy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/RLWC_trophy.jpg/300px-RLWC_trophy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1181" data-file-height="1772" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RLWC_trophy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Paul_Barri%C3%A8re" title="Paul Barrière">Paul Barrière</a> Trophy first awarded in the 1954 inaugural contest.</div></div></div>
<p>The World Cup trophy was commissioned by French <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Fran%C3%A7aise_de_Rugby_%C3%A0_XIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Fédération Française de Rugby à XIII">Fédération Française de Rugby à XIII</a> president <a href="/wiki/Paul_Barri%C3%A8re" title="Paul Barrière">Paul Barrière</a> at a cost of eight million francs, and then donated to the <a href="/wiki/International_Rugby_League_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="International Rugby League Board">International Rugby League Board</a> to be used for the inaugural competition in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-RLIF1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RLIF1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This trophy was used and presented to the winning nation for the first four tournaments, before being stolen in 1970. After its recovery, the trophy was reinstated for the 2000 tournament.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualification">Qualification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Qualification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rugby_league_world_cup_countries.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/Rugby_league_world_cup_countries.png/300px-Rugby_league_world_cup_countries.png" width="300" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/Rugby_league_world_cup_countries.png/450px-Rugby_league_world_cup_countries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/Rugby_league_world_cup_countries.png/600px-Rugby_league_world_cup_countries.png 2x" data-file-width="867" data-file-height="402" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rugby_league_world_cup_countries.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rugby league World Cup countries for the 2017 tournament</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/National_team_appearances_at_Rugby_League_World_Cups" title="National team appearances at Rugby League World Cups">National team appearances at Rugby League World Cups</a></div>
<p>Australia, France and New Zealand are the only nations who have appeared at every Rugby League World Cup from 1954 to 2013. England has also been at all, but participated under the banner of Great Britain in the majority of the earlier tournaments. Wales, including as Great Britain, has competed in all but the 2008 tournament.
</p><p>In total, 19 teams have taken part in the world cup.  While 18 of these represented nations, 1 did not; in 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Aotearoa_M%C4%81ori" class="mw-redirect" title="Aotearoa Māori">Aotearoa Māori</a> team was granted entry to the competition.  This team is made up of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_M%C4%81ori_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand Māori rugby league team">New Zealand Māori</a> players and was knocked out of the world cup in the pool stage.  Only one other team has taken part in just a single world cup; <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Russia national rugby league team">Russia</a>. In total 29 teams have/will taken part in qualifying rounds while 5 other teams have always been granted automatic qualification, meaning 34 teams have taken part in some stage of the world cup.
</p><p>Qualifying rounds were first introduced for the <a href="/wiki/2000_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2000 Rugby League World Cup">2000 world cup</a>.  Rounds take the form of groups of teams from specific continents/regions; Europe, Africa/middle-east, Asia/pacific and the Americas.  Teams that automatically qualify are the quarter-finalists from the previous world cup.  
</p><p>Qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/2021_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2021 Rugby League World Cup">2021 world cup</a> will feature 20 teams, the most to date with 8 teams having automatically qualified.  13 of these teams have never qualified for the world cup with the possibility of 7 of these debutants to reach the tournament proper.  14 teams will take part in the European stage of the qualifying with 4 teams in the Americas group and 3 in the world play-offs where the runner-up of the Americas group will meet the highest ranked teams from Asia/pacific and Africa/middle-east.      
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finals">Finals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Finals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Rugby League World Cup has followed a varied range of formats throughout its history as the number of teams participating has increased.
</p><p>The current format has been in use since 2013 featuring 14 teams split into two groups of four and two groups of three. Three teams from the groups of four qualify for the knockout stage and one team from the groups of three qualify. Each team is awarded two points for a win and one point for a draw.
</p><p>The eight teams in the quarter finals play each other with the four winners progressing to the semi finals before the World Cup Final. If the teams are level after 80 minutes extra time will be played and if the two teams are still level after extra time, a golden point will be played.
</p><p>In 2017 the final tournament followed the same format as that of 2013 but this will change for 2021 when the number of teams taking part is increased to 16.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hosts">Hosts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hosts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup_hosts" title="Rugby League World Cup hosts">Rugby League World Cup hosts</a></div>
<p>Seven teams have officially hosted and co-hosted the World Cup.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Only <a href="/wiki/1975_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1975 Rugby League World Cup">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9388_Rugby_League_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="1985–88 Rugby League World Cup">1985-88</a> and <a href="/wiki/1989-92_Rugby_League_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="1989-92 Rugby League World Cup">1989-92</a> were held internationally and not in a specific country. <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> hosted games in the 2000 world cup but these games were considered to have been hosted by <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> rather than the specific home nations. Although games were played in <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> during the 1985-88 and 1989-92 World Cups, they are due to officially become the eighth nation to host games in 2017 alongside <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadiums">Stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup_venues" title="Rugby League World Cup venues">Rugby League World Cup venues</a></div>
<p>In total, 81 stadiums have hosted world cup games over the 14 tournaments. <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Carnegie_Rugby_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Headingley Carnegie Rugby Stadium">Headingley Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> has hosted the tournament the most times, having had games in 7 world cups with <a href="/wiki/Central_Park_(Wigan)" title="Central Park (Wigan)">Central Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wigan" title="Wigan">Wigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lang_Park" title="Lang Park">Lang Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> having hosted 6 tournaments.  52 stadiums have hosted matches in just 1 tournament.  The most stadiums used in a tournament was in 2000 when 26 stadiums were used; the stadium capacity was the highest ever at 704,400. However, the occupancy was also the lowest ever at just 37.46%.
</p><p>The largest stadium in terms of capacity ever used was <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> with a seating capacity of 90,000; the stadium was used in the 2013 tournament as the venue for the semi-final double-header. The smallest stadium ever used was also in 2013 when <a href="/wiki/The_Gnoll" title="The Gnoll">The Gnoll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neath" title="Neath">Neath</a>, with a capacity of 5,000 hosted a game between <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands_national_rugby_league_team" title="Cook Islands national rugby league team">Cook Islands</a>. Despite this, it was not the lowest attended game; this was in the 2000 world cup when just 1,497 attended the game between <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon_national_rugby_league_team" title="Lebanon national rugby league team">Lebanon</a> at <a href="/wiki/Stradey_Park" title="Stradey Park">Stradey Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Llanelli" title="Llanelli">Llanelli</a>.
</p><p>The city with the most stadiums used is <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> with 4. <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> are the cities with the next highest number with 3 each.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Successful_nations">Successful nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rugby_League_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Successful nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Up to and including the 2017 tournament only Australia, New Zealand and Great Britain had been crowned World Champions with Australia easily the most successful, winning 11 of 15 tournaments. Great Britain have won three times, and New Zealand once. New Zealand have also finished runners-up in three World Cups, while France have been runners-up twice, including the inaugural cup where they were captained by <a href="/wiki/Puig_Aubert" title="Puig Aubert">Puig Aubert</a>. England have also finished runners-up three times, while the Great Britain team were runners-up four times. Fiji have reached the semi-finals three times, while Wales also made the semi-final in 1995 and 2000. Ireland and Samoa have twice made it past the qualifying pool stages. Other nations to have proceeded to the knock-out stages are Papua New Guinea, Scotland, the United States, and Lebanon.
</p>
